<p><b>Marshallese</b> (Marshallese: <i lang="mh">Kajin M̧ajel‌̧</i> or <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kajin Majōl</i></span> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[kɑzʲinʲ(i)mˠɑːzʲɛlˠ]</a></span>), also known as <b>Ebon</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Micronesian language">Micronesian language</a> spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>. The language of the <a href="/wiki/Marshallese_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshallese people">Marshallese people</a>, it is spoken by nearly all of the country's population of 59,000, making it the principal language.<sup id="cite_ref-Pop_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pop-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> There are also roughly 27,000 Marshallese citizens residing in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ruststaff_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruststaff-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> nearly all of whom speak Marshallese, as well as residents in other countries such as <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>.
</p><p>There are two major dialects, the western <a href="/wiki/Ralik_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ralik Chain">Rālik</a> and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Ratak_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ratak Chain">Ratak</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Marshallese, a <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_languages" title="Micronesian languages">Micronesian language</a>, is a member of the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic</a> subgroup of the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The closest linguistic relatives of Marshallese are the other Micronesian languages, including <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_language" title="Nauruan language">Nauruan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pohnpeian_language" title="Pohnpeian language">Pohnpeian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mokilese_language" title="Mokilese language">Mokilese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuukese_language" title="Chuukese language">Chuukese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolinian_people" title="Carolinian people">Refaluwash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kosraean_language" title="Kosraean language">Kosraean</a>. Marshallese shows 50% lexical similarity with <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mokilese_language" title="Mokilese language">Mokilese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pohnpeian_language" title="Pohnpeian language">Pohnpeian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within the <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesian</a> archipelago, Marshallese—along with the rest of the Micronesian language group—is not as closely related to the more ambiguously classified Oceanic language <a href="/wiki/Yapese_language" title="Yapese language">Yapese</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yap_State" title="Yap State">Yap State</a>, or to the <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_outlier" title="Polynesian outlier">Polynesian outlier</a> languages <a href="/wiki/Kapingamarangi_language" title="Kapingamarangi language">Kapingamarangi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nukuoro_language" title="Nukuoro language">Nukuoro</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pohnpei_State" title="Pohnpei State">Pohnpei State</a>, and even less closely related to the non-Oceanic languages <a href="/wiki/Palauan_language" title="Palauan language">Palauan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">Chamorro</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variation">Variation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Variation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Marshall_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Marshall Islands">Republic of the Marshall Islands</a> contains 34 <a href="/wiki/Atolls" class="mw-redirect" title="Atolls">atolls</a> that are split into two chains, the eastern <a href="/wiki/Ratak_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ratak Chain">Ratak Chain</a> and the western <a href="/wiki/R%C4%81lik_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Rālik Chain">Rālik Chain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> These two chains have different dialects, which differ mainly <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">lexically</a>, and are <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The atoll of <a href="/wiki/Ujelang" class="mw-redirect" title="Ujelang">Ujelang</a> in the west was reported to have "slightly less homogeneous speech",<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> but it has been uninhabited since 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Ratak and Rālik dialects differ phonetically in how they deal with stems that begin with double consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Ratak Marshallese inserts a vowel to separate the consonants, while Ralik adds a vowel before the consonants (and pronounced an unwritten consonant phoneme <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> before the vowel).<sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> For example, the stem <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kkure</i></span> 'play' becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ikkure</i></span> in Rālik Marshallese and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kukure</i></span> in Ratak Marshallese.<sup id="cite_ref-hgb_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgb-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Status"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_(Marshallese).pdf" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf/page1-220px-Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="285" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf/page1-330px-Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf/page1-440px-Stop_the_Spread_of_Germs_updated_%28Marshallese%29.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1275" data-file-height="1650" /></a><figcaption>A poster sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">CDC</a> about <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19</a> prevention in Marshallese.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Marshallese is the official language of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> and enjoys vigorous use.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> As of 1979, the language was spoken by 43,900 people in the Marshall Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> in 2020 the number was closer to 59,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Pop_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pop-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Additional groups of speakers in other countries including <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> increase the total number of Marshallese speakers, with approximately 27,000 Marshallese-Americans living in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ruststaff_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruststaff-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/Pohnpeian_language" title="Pohnpeian language">Pohnpeian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuukese_language" title="Chuukese language">Chuukese</a>, Marshallese stands out among Micronesian languages in having tens of thousands of speakers; most Micronesian languages have far fewer.<sup id="cite_ref-w2008pp6-7_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w2008pp6-7-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> A dictionary and at least two Bible translations have been published in Marshallese.<sup id="cite_ref-eth_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eth-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Marshallese has a large consonant inventory, and each consonant has some type of secondary articulation (<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">palatalization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">velarization</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">rounding</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-w1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The palatalized consonants are regarded as "light", and the velarized and rounded consonants are regarded as "heavy", with the rounded consonants being both velarized and <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">labialized</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> (This contrast is similar to that between "slender" and "broad" consonants in <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Goidelic languages</a>, or between "soft" and "hard" consonants in <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a>.) The "light" consonants are considered more relaxed articulations.
<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">ŋʷ</a></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">Rhotic</a>
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>

</td>
<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">rˠ</a></span>
</td>

</td>

</th>

</td>

<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">lʲ</a></span>
</td>

<th><a href="/wiki/Glide_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Glide consonant">Glide</a>
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_approximant" title="Voiced palatal approximant">j</a></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>(<span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_approximant" title="Voiced velar approximant">ɰ</a></span>)
</td>
<td><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Voiced_labial%E2%80%93velar_approximant" title="Voiced labial–velar approximant">w</a></span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Although Marshallese has no <a href="/wiki/Consonant_voicing_and_devoicing" title="Consonant voicing and devoicing">voicing</a> contrast in consonants,<sup id="cite_ref-w1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> stops may be allophonically <a href="/wiki/Partial_voicing" class="mw-redirect" title="Partial voicing">partially voiced</a> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[p<span class="wrap"> </span>→<span class="wrap"> </span>b]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t<span class="wrap"> </span>→<span class="wrap"> </span>d]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k<span class="wrap"> </span>→<span class="wrap"> </span>ɡ]</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> when they are between vowels and not <a href="/wiki/Geminated" class="mw-redirect" title="Geminated">geminated</a>. (Technically, partially voiced stops would be <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[p̬~b̥]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t̬~d̥]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k̬~ɡ̊]</span>, but this article uses voiced transcriptions <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_plosive" title="Voiced bilabial plosive">b</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_plosive" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar plosive">d</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_plosive" title="Voiced velar plosive">ɡ</a>&#93;</span> for simplicity.)<sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Final consonants are often <a href="/wiki/Unreleased_stop" class="mw-redirect" title="Unreleased stop">unreleased</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Glides <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j<span class="wrap"> </span>ɰ<span class="wrap"> </span>w/</span> vanish in many environments, with surrounding vowels assimilating their <a href="/wiki/Backness" class="mw-redirect" title="Backness">backness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roundedness" title="Roundedness">roundedness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-b21-22_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b21-22-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> That is motivated by the limited surface distribution of these phonemes as well as other evidence that backness and roundedness are not specified phonemically for Marshallese vowels.<sup id="cite_ref-b21-22_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b21-22-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In fact, the consonant <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɰ/</span> never surfaces phonetically but is used to explain the preceding phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> may surface phonetically in word-initial and word-final positions and, even then, not consistently.<sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>)
</p><p>Bender (1968) explains that it was once believed there were six bilabial consonants because of observed surface realizations, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p<span class="wrap"> </span>pʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>pʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>m<span class="wrap"> </span>mʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʷ/</span>, but he determined that two of these, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p<span class="wrap"> </span>m/</span>, were actually allophones of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʲ/</span> respectively before front vowels and allophones of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠ/</span> respectively before back vowels.<sup id="cite_ref-b16_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b16-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Before front vowels, the velarized <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant" title="Labial consonant">labial consonants</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠ/</span> actually tend to have rounded (labiovelarized) articulations <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʷ]</span>, but they remain unrounded on the phonemic level, and there are no distinct <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʷ/</span> phonemes.<sup id="cite_ref-b16_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b16-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bxvi-xvii_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bxvi-xvii-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The pronunciation guide used by <i>Naan</i> (2014) still recognizes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[p<span class="wrap"> </span>m]</span> as allophone symbols separate from <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>pˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠ]</span> in these same conditions while recognizing that there are only palatalized and velarized phonemes.<sup id="cite_ref-naan_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naan-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This article uses <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>pˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>mʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠ]</span> in phonetic transcriptions.
</p><p>The consonant <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʲ/</span> may be phonetically realized as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">tʲ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t͡sʲ]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">sʲ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[t͡ɕ]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal fricative">ɕ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_plosive" title="Voiceless palatal plosive">c</a>&#93;</span>, or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">ç</a>&#93;</span> (or any of their <a href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced consonant">voiced</a> variants <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">dʲ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[d͡zʲ]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">zʲ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[d͡ʑ]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal fricative">ʑ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_plosive" title="Voiced palatal plosive">ɟ</a>&#93;</span>, or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative" title="Voiced palatal fricative">ʝ</a>&#93;</span>), in <a href="/wiki/Free_variation" title="Free variation">free variation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Word-internally it usually assumes a <a href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced consonant">voiced</a> <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Fricative consonant">fricative</a> articulation as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">zʲ</a>&#93;</span> (or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal fricative">ʑ</a>&#93;</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative" title="Voiced palatal fricative">ʝ</a>&#93;</span>) but not when <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">geminated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʲ/</span> is used to adapt foreign <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">sibilants</a> into Marshallese. In phonetic transcription, this article uses <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">tʲ</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">zʲ</a>&#93;</span> as voiceless and voiced allophones of the same phoneme.
</p><p>Marshallese has no distinct <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʷ/</span> phoneme.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dorsal_consonant" title="Dorsal consonant">dorsal consonants</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>kʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋʷ/</span> are usually <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">velar</a> but with the tongue a little farther back <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k̠<span class="wrap"> </span>ɡ̠<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋ̠<span class="wrap"> </span>k̠ʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɡ̠ʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋ̠ʷ]</span>, making them somewhere between velar and <a href="/wiki/Uvular_consonant" title="Uvular consonant">uvular</a> in articulation.<sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> All dorsal phonemes are "heavy" (velarized or rounded), and none are "light" (palatalized).<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As stated before, the <a href="/wiki/Palatal_consonant" title="Palatal consonant">palatal consonant</a> articulations <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_plosive" title="Voiceless palatal plosive">c</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_plosive" title="Voiced palatal plosive">ɟ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">ç</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative" title="Voiced palatal fricative">ʝ</a>&#93;</span> are treated as allophones of the palatalized <i><a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">coronal</a></i> obstruent <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʲ/</span>, even though palatal consonants are physically dorsal. For simplicity, this article uses unmarked <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k<span class="wrap"> </span>ɡ<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>kʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɡʷ<span class="wrap"> </span>ŋʷ]</span> in phonetic transcription.
</p><p>Bender (1969) describes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nˠ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʷ/</span> as being 'dark' <i>r</i>-colored, but is not more specific.<sup id="cite_ref-bxvii_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bxvii-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Marshallese-English Dictionary (MED) describes these as heavy <a href="/wiki/Dental_nasal" class="mw-redirect" title="Dental nasal">dental nasals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Consonants <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rˠ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rʷ/</span> are all <a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">coronal consonants</a> and full <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">trills</a>. <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rˠ/</span> is similar to <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">rr</i></span> with a trill position just behind the <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Alveolar ridge">alveolar ridge</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Postalveolar trill">postalveolar trill</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[r̠ˠ]</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-bxvii_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bxvii-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> but <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rʲ/</span> is a palatalized <a href="/wiki/Dental_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Dental trill">dental trill</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[r̪ʲ]</span>, articulated further forward behind the <a href="/wiki/Front_teeth" class="mw-redirect" title="Front teeth">front teeth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The MED and Willson (2003) describe the rhotic consonants as "<a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex</a>", but are not clear how this relates to their dental or alveolar trill positions.<sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-w6_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w6-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Retroflex trill">retroflex trill</a>.) This article uses <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">rʲ</a>&#93;</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">rˠ</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">rʷ</a>&#93;</span> in phonetic transcription.
</p><p>The heavy lateral consonants <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lˠ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lʷ/</span> are <a href="/wiki/Dark_l" class="mw-redirect" title="Dark l">dark <i>l</i></a> like in English <i>feel</i>, articulated <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Velarized_alveolar_lateral_approximant" class="mw-redirect" title="Velarized alveolar lateral approximant">ɫ</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">ɫʷ</a>&#93;</span> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-alph_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alph-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This article uses <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Velarized_alveolar_lateral_approximant" class="mw-redirect" title="Velarized alveolar lateral approximant">lˠ</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">lʷ</a>&#93;</span> in phonetic transcription.
</p><p>The velarized consonants (and, by extension, the rounded consonants) may be velarized or <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a><sup id="cite_ref-MEDSounds_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDSounds-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> like the <a href="/wiki/Emphatic_consonant" title="Emphatic consonant">emphatic consonants</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mizrahi_Hebrew" title="Mizrahi Hebrew">Mizrahi Hebrew</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vowels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Marshallese has a <a href="/wiki/Vertical_vowel_system" title="Vertical vowel system">vertical vowel system</a> of just four <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a>, each with several <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophones</a> depending on the surrounding consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-w2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w2-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the phonemic level, while Bender (1969) and Choi (1992) agree that the vowel phonemes are distinguished by <a href="/wiki/Vowel_height" class="mw-redirect" title="Vowel height">height</a>, they describe the abstract nature of these phonemes differently, with Bender treating the <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front</a> unrounded surface realizations as their relaxed state that becomes altered by proximity of velarized or rounded consonants,<sup id="cite_ref-bxiii-xvii_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bxiii-xvii-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> while Choi uses <a href="/wiki/Central_vowel" title="Central vowel">central vowel</a> symbols in a neutral fashion to notate the abstract phonemes and completely different <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front</a>, <a href="/wiki/Back_vowel" title="Back vowel">back</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roundedness" title="Roundedness">rounded</a> vowel symbols for surface realizations. Bender (1968, 1969), MED (1976) and Willson (2003) recognize four vowel phonemes, but Choi (1992) observes only three of the phonemes as having a stable quality, but theorizes that there may be a historical process of reduction from four to three, and otherwise ignores the fourth phoneme. For phonemic transcription of vowels, this article recognizes four phonemes and uses the front unrounded vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɛ<span class="wrap"> </span>e<span class="wrap"> </span>i/</span> notation of the MED, following the approach of Bender (1969) in treating the front vowel surface realizations as the representative phonemes.
</p><p>On the phonetic level, Bender (1968), MED (1976), Choi (1992), Willson (2003) and <i>Naan</i> (2014) notate some Marshallese vowel surface realizations differently from one another, and they disagree on how to characterize the <a href="/wiki/Vowel_height" class="mw-redirect" title="Vowel height">vowel heights</a> of the underlying phonemes, with Willson (2003) taking the most divergent approach in treating the four heights as actually two heights each with the added presence (+ATR) or absence (-ATR) of <a href="/wiki/Advanced_tongue_root" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced tongue root">advanced tongue root</a>. Bender (1968) assigns central vowel symbols for the surface realizations that neighbor velarized consonants, but the MED (1976), Choi (1992) and Willson (2003) largely assign back unrounded vowel symbols for these, with the exception that the MED uses <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Mid_central_vowel" title="Mid central vowel">ə</a>&#93;</span> rather than cardinal <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back unrounded vowel">ɤ</a>&#93;</span> for the <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back unrounded vowel">close-mid back unrounded vowel</a>, and Choi (1992) and Willson (2003) use <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a>&#93;</span> rather than cardinal <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">ɑ</a>&#93;</span> for the <a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">open back unrounded vowel</a>. <i>Naan</i> (2014) is the only reference providing a <a href="/wiki/Vowel_trapezium" class="mw-redirect" title="Vowel trapezium">vowel trapezium</a> for its own vowels, and differs especially from the other vowel models in splitting the front allophones of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> into two realizations (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-close_near-front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-close near-front unrounded vowel">ɪ</a>&#93;</span> before consonants and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">i</a>&#93;</span> in open syllables), merging the front allophones of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span> as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">ɛ</a>&#93;</span> before consonants and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">e</a>&#93;</span> in open syllables, merging the rounded allophones of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span> as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">o</a>&#93;</span>, and indicating the front allophone of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ/</span> as a close-mid central unrounded vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid central unrounded vowel">ɘ</a>&#93;</span>, a realization more raised even than the front allophone of the normally higher <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>. For phonetic notation of vowel surface realizations, this article largely uses the MED's notation, but uses only cardinal symbols for back unrounded vowels.
</p>

<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a>&#93;</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">ɔ</a>&#93;</span>
</td>
<td><span class="nowrap">-hi, -ATR</span>
</td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">ɛ</a>&#93;</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a>&#93;</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">ɔ</a>&#93;</span>
</td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close-mid_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid central unrounded vowel">ë</a>&#93;</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a>&#93;</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">ɒ</a>&#93;</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Superficially, 12 Marshallese vowel allophones appear in <a href="/wiki/Minimal_pairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Minimal pairs">minimal pairs</a>, a common test for phonemicity.<sup id="cite_ref-b17_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b17-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> For example, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mʲæ]</span> (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">mā</i></span>, 'breadfruit'), <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mʲɑ]</span> (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ma</i></span>, 'but'), and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mʲɒ]</span> (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">mo̧</i></span>, 'taboo') are separate Marshallese words.<sup id="cite_ref-b17_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b17-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, the uneven distribution of glide phonemes suggests that they underlyingly end with the glides (thus <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mʲæj/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mʲæɰ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mʲæw/</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-b21-22_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b21-22-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> When glides are taken into account, it emerges that there are only 4 vowel phonemes.<sup id="cite_ref-b21-22_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b21-22-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When a vowel phoneme appears between consonants with different secondary articulations, the vowel often surfaces as a smooth transition from one vowel allophone to the other.<sup id="cite_ref-w3_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> For example, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jok</i></span> 'shy', phonemically <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʲɛkʷ/</span>, is often realized phonetically as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʲɛ͡ɔkʷ]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-w3_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It follows that there are 24 possible short <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a> in Marshallese:<sup id="cite_ref-w3_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;" align="center">

</th>

<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɒ͡æ]</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɒ͡ɑ]</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>These diphthongs are the typical realizations of short vowels between two non-glide consonants, but in reality the diphthongs themselves are not phonemic, and short vowels between two consonants with different secondary articulations can be articulated as either a smooth diphthong (such as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ͡ʌ]</span>) or as a monophthong of one of the two vowel allophones (such as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ʌ]</span>), all in free variation. Bender (1968) also observes that when the would-be diphthong starts with a back rounded vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɒ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɔ<span class="wrap"> </span>o<span class="wrap"> </span>u]</span> and ends with a front unrounded vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[æ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɛ<span class="wrap"> </span>e<span class="wrap"> </span>i]</span>, then a vowel allophone associated with the back unrounded vowels (notated in this article as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑ<span class="wrap"> </span>ʌ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɤ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɯ]</span>) may also occur in the vowel nucleus.<sup id="cite_ref-b22-23_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-23-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Because the cumulative visual complexity of notating so many diphthongs in phonetic transcriptions can make them more difficult to read, it is not uncommon to phonetically transcribe Marshallese vowel allophones only as one predominant monophthongal allophone, so that a word like <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʲɛ͡ɔkʷ]</span> can be more simply transcribed as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʲɔkʷ]</span>, in a condensed fashion. Before Bender's (1968) discovery that Marshallese utilized a vertical vowel system, it was conventional to transcribe the language in this manner with a presumed inventory of 12 vowel monophthong phonemes,<sup id="cite_ref-b17-21_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b17-21-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and it remains in occasional use as a more condensed phonetic transcription.<sup id="cite_ref-c22-25_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c22-25-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-w6_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w6-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> This article uses phonemic or diphthongal phonetic transcriptions for illustrative purposes, but for most examples it uses condensed phonetic transcription with the most relevant short vowel allophones roughly corresponding to <a href="#Orthography">Marshallese orthography</a> as informed by the MED.
</p><p>Some syllables appear to contain long vowels: <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">naaj</i></span> 'future'.<sup id="cite_ref-w7_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> They are thought to contain an underlying glide (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɰ/</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span>), which is not present phonetically.<sup id="cite_ref-w7-8_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-8-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-b22_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> For instance, the underlying form of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">naaj</i></span> is <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʲæɰætʲ/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-w7_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Although the medial glide is not realized phonetically, it affects vowel quality; in a word like <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʲæɰætʲ/</span>, the vowel transitions from <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">æ</a>&#93;</span> to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">ɑ</a>&#93;</span> and then back to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">æ</a>&#93;</span>, as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nʲæ͡ɑɑ͡ætʲ]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-clong_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clong-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In condensed phonetic transcription, the same word can be expressed as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nʲɑɑtʲ]</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nʲɑːtʲ]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-b17-21_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b17-21-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-c22-25_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c22-25-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-w6_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w6-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonotactics">Phonotactics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Phonotactics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Syllables in Marshallese follow CV, CVC, and VC patterns.<sup id="cite_ref-w7_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Marshallese words always underlyingly begin and end with consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-b22_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Initial, final, and long vowels may be explained as the results of underlying glides not present on the phonetic level.<sup id="cite_ref-b22_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Initial vowels are sometimes realized with an onglide <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_approximant" title="Voiced palatal approximant">j</a>&#93;</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_labial%E2%80%93velar_approximant" title="Voiced labial–velar approximant">w</a>&#93;</span> but not consistently:<sup id="cite_ref-c22_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c22-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jætʲ/<span class="wrap"> </span>→<span class="wrap"> </span>[ætʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>jætʲ]</span> 'weave'<sup id="cite_ref-c23_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c23-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Only <a href="/wiki/Homorganic_consonants" class="mw-redirect" title="Homorganic consonants">homorganic</a> consonant sequences are allowed in Marshallese,<sup id="cite_ref-w4-5_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w4-5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> including geminate varieties of each consonant, except for glides.<sup id="cite_ref-c14_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c14-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Non-homorganic clusters are separated by vowel <a href="/wiki/Epenthesis" title="Epenthesis">epenthesis</a> even across word boundaries.<sup id="cite_ref-w4-5_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w4-5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Some homorganic clusters are also disallowed:<sup id="cite_ref-w4-5_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w4-5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Obstruent_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Obstruent consonant">Obstruent</a>-obstruent, <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">nasal</a>-nasal, <a href="/wiki/Liquid_consonant" title="Liquid consonant">liquid</a>-liquid, nasal-obstruent, and nasal-liquid clusters undergo assimilation of the secondary articulation except if the first consonant is a rounded coronal or a rounded dorsal. Then, the clusters undergo assimilation of the rounded articulation.<sup id="cite_ref-w5_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w5-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>†Obstruent-liquid and liquid-obstruent clusters besides <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lʲtˠ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lˠtˠ/</span> undergo epenthesis.<sup id="cite_ref-w5_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w5-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Liquid-nasal clusters undergo nasal assimilation.<sup id="cite_ref-w5_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w5-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Obstruent-nasal clusters undergo epenthesis (if coronal) or nasal assimilation (if non-coronal).<sup id="cite_ref-w5_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w5-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Clusters involving any glides undergo epenthesis, including otherwise homorganic clusters of two of the same glide.</li></ul>
<p>The following assimilations are created, with empty combinations representing epenthesis.
</p>

<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rː/</span>
</td>

</th>

</td>
<th><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/◌ʲ/</span>

<td rowspan="2"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/◌ˠ◌ˠ/</span>

<td rowspan="2"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/◌ʷ◌ʷ/</span>
</td></tr>

</th></tr>
<tr align="center">
<th><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/◌ʷ/</span>
</th>
<td colspan="3"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/◌ʷ◌ʷ/</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vowel_height" class="mw-redirect" title="Vowel height">vowel height</a> of an epenthetic vowel is not phonemic as the epenthetic vowel itself is not phonemic, but is still phonetically predictable given the two nearest other vowels and whether one or both of the cluster consonants are glides.<sup id="cite_ref-b22_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-w7_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Bender (1968) does not specifically explain the vowel heights of epenthetic vowels between two non-glides, but of his various examples containing such vowels, none of the epenthetic vowels has a height lower than the highest of either of their nearest neighboring vowels, and the epenthetic vowel actually becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̯/</span> if the two nearest vowels are both <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ/</span>. <i>Naan</i> (2014) does not take the heights of epenthetic vowels between non-glides into consideration, phonetically transcribing all of them as a <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Mid_central_vowel" title="Mid central vowel">ə</a>&#93;</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-naan_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naan-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> But when one of the consonants in a cluster is a glide, the height of the epenthetic vowel between them follows a different process, assuming the same height of whichever vowel is on the opposite side of that glide, forming a long vowel with it across the otherwise silent glide.<sup id="cite_ref-b22-23_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b22-23-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Epenthetic vowels do not effect the rhythm of the spoken language, and can never be a stressed syllable.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Phonetic transcription may indicate epenthetic vowels between two non-glides as non-syllabic,<sup id="cite_ref-b8_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b8-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> using IPA notation similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Semi-vowel" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-vowel">semi-vowels</a>. Certain Westernized Marshallese placenames spell out the epenthetic vowels:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ebeye" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebeye">Ebeye</a>, from earlier <i>Eb<b>e</b>je</i>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Epjā</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erikub" class="mw-redirect" title="Erikub">Er<b>i</b>kub</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ādkup</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kwajalein" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwajalein">Kwaj<b>a</b>lein</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kuwajleen</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Majuro" title="Majuro">Maj<b>u</b>ro</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Mājro</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Namorik" class="mw-redirect" title="Namorik">Nam<b>o</b>rik</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Nam̧dik</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Omelek" class="mw-redirect" title="Omelek">Om<b>e</b>lek</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kom̧le</i></span> ("<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">K<u>om̧le, K</u>om̧le</i></span>")<sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rongelap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rongelap">Rong<b>e</b>lap</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ron̄l‌̧ap</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rongerik" class="mw-redirect" title="Rongerik">Rong<b>e</b>rik</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ron̄dik</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ujelang" class="mw-redirect" title="Ujelang">Uj<b>e</b>lang</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Wūjlan̄</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Uliga" title="Uliga">Ul<b>i</b>ga</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Wūlka</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Utirik" class="mw-redirect" title="Utirik">Ut<b>i</b>rik</a>, from <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Utrōk</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Epenthetic vowels in general can be omitted without affecting meaning, such as in song or in enunciated syllable breaks. This article uses non-syllabic notation in phonetic IPA transcription to indicate epenthetic vowels between non-glides.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timing">Timing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Timing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The short vowel phonemes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ<span class="wrap"> </span>ɛ<span class="wrap"> </span>e<span class="wrap"> </span>i/</span> and the approximant phonemes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j<span class="wrap"> </span>ɰ<span class="wrap"> </span>w/</span> all occupy a roughly equal duration of time.<sup id="cite_ref-c27_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c27-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Though they occupy time, the approximants are generally not articulated as glides, and Choi (1992) does not rule out a deeper level of representation.<sup id="cite_ref-c71_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c71-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In particular, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/V/</span> short vowels occupy one unit of time, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/VGV/</span> long vowels (for which <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/G/</span> is an approximant phoneme) are three times as long.<sup id="cite_ref-c65_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c65-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a matter of <a href="/wiki/Prosody_(linguistics)" title="Prosody (linguistics)">prosody</a>, each <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/C/</span> consonant and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/V/</span> vowel phonemic sequence carries one <a href="/wiki/Mora_(linguistics)" title="Mora (linguistics)">mora</a> in length, with the exception of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/C/</span> in <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV/</span> sequences where the vowel carries one mora for both phonemes. All morae are thus measured in <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV/</span> or shut <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/C/</span> sequences:<sup id="cite_ref-w8_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w8-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CVC/</span> is two morae: <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV-C/</span>. It is also the shortest possible length of a Marshallese word.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CVCVC/</span> is three morae: <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV-CV-C/</span>. Since approximants are also consonants, long vowel sequences of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CVGVC/</span> are also three morae.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CVCCVC/</span> is four morae: <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV-C-CV-C/</span>.</li>
<li>Prefixes like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ri-</i></span> are <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/CV-/</span> sequences occupying only one mora but are attached to words rather than standing as words on their own.</li>
<li>Suffixes like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">-in</i></span> are <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/-VC/</span> sequences. The syllable itself occupies two morae but adds only one mora to the word because the vowel attaches itself to the last consonant phoneme in the word, changing <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/-C/</span> into <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/-C‿V-C/</span>.</li></ul>
<p>That makes Marshallese a mora-rhythmed language in a fashion similar to <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sound_changes">Historic sound changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Historic sound changes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">∅</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rʲ/</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rˠ,<span class="wrap"> </span>rʷ/</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lʲ,<span class="wrap"> </span>lˠ,<span class="wrap"> </span>lʷ/</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʲ,<span class="wrap"> </span>nˠ,<span class="wrap"> </span>nʷ/</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʲ/</span>
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Marshallese consonants show splits conditioned by the surrounding Proto-Micronesian vowels. Proto-Micronesian *k *ŋ *r become rounded next to *o or next to *u except in bisyllables whose other vowel is unrounded. Default outcomes of *l and *n are palatalized; they become velarized or rounded before *a or sometimes *o if there is no high vowel in an adjacent syllable. Then, roundedness is determined by the same rule as above.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg/220px-Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="288" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg/330px-Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg/440px-Book_of_Mormon_-_Marshallese.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2513" data-file-height="3290" /></a><figcaption>Marshallese version of the <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Mormon" title="Book of Mormon">Book of Mormon</a></i></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alphabet_marshallais.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Alphabet_marshallais.jpg/220px-Alphabet_marshallais.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Alphabet_marshallais.jpg/330px-Alphabet_marshallais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Alphabet_marshallais.jpg/440px-Alphabet_marshallais.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Marshallese alphabet in a library</figcaption></figure>
<p>Marshallese is written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>. There are two competing orthographies.<sup id="cite_ref-mx_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mx-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The "old" orthography was introduced by missionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-mx_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mx-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> This system is not highly consistent or faithful in representing the sounds of Marshallese, but until recently, it had no competing orthography.<sup id="cite_ref-r6_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r6-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It is currently widely used, including in newspapers and signs.<sup id="cite_ref-r6_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r6-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The "new" orthography is gaining popularity especially in schools and among young adults and children.<sup id="cite_ref-mx_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mx-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The "new" orthography represents the sounds of the Marshallese language more faithfully and is the system used in the Marshallese–English dictionary by Abo et al., currently the only complete published Marshallese dictionary.<sup id="cite_ref-mx_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mx-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-r6_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r6-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Here is the current <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">alphabet</a>, as promoted by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Marshall_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Marshall Islands">Republic of the Marshall Islands</a>. It consists of 24 letters.
</p>

</th>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā</i></span></td>
