</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Marshallese spelling is based on pronunciation rather than a phonemic analysis. Therefore, backness is marked in vowels despite being allophonic (it does not change the meaning), and many instances of the glides <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j<span class="wrap"> </span>ɰ<span class="wrap"> </span>w/</span> proposed on the phonemic level are unwritten, because they do not surface as consonants phonetically. In particular, the glide <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɰ/</span>, which never surfaces as a consonant phonetically, is always unwritten.
</p><p>The letter <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">w</i></span> is generally used only in three situations:
</p>
<ol><li>To mark a rounded consonant (one of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kw l‌̧w n‌̧w n̄w rw</i></span>) or approximant phoneme (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">w</i></span>) before a vowel that precedes an unrounded consonant phoneme (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a ā e i ō ū</i></span>). Even then, if the consonant phoneme comes after a back rounded vowel <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">o̧ o u</i></span> and before another vowel, it is common to write one of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧ n‌̧ r</i></span> instead of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧w n‌̧w rw</i></span>, but the rounded dorsal consonants <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kw n̄w</i></span> are still written with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">w</i></span> in these circumstances.</li>
<li>To mark a velarized bilabial consonant (either <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">bw</i></span> or <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">m̧w</i></span>) before a vowel that precedes a palatalized consonant phoneme (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā e i</i></span>).</li>
<li>To indicate a <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_labial%E2%80%93velar_approximant" title="Voiced labial–velar approximant">w</a>&#93;</span> glide phonetically surfacing either word-initially or between two vowels.</li></ol>
<p><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">w</i></span> is never written out word-finally or before another consonant.
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kuwajleen / Kuajleen</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʷuwɑzʲɛ̆lʲɛːnʲ]</span> "<a href="/wiki/Kwajalein" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwajalein">Kwajalein</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The palatal glide phoneme <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> may also be written out but only as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> before one of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a o ō o̧</i></span>, or as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> before one of either <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">u ū</i></span>. The approximant is never written before any of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā e i</i></span>. A stronger raised palatal glide <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">i̯</a>&#93;</span>, phonemically analyzed as the exotic un-syllabic consonant-vowel-consonant sequence <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ji̯j/</span> rather than plain <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>, may occur word-initially before any vowel and is written <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span>. For historical reasons, certain words like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe</i></span> may be written as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">yokwe</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-medYokwe_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medYokwe-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> with a <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">y</i></span>, which does not otherwise exist in the Marshallese alphabet.
</p><p>One source of orthographic variation is in the representation of vowels. Pure <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongs</a> are written consistently based on vowel quality. However, short <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a> may often be written with one of the two vowel sounds that they contain. (Alternate phonetic realizations for the same phonemic sequences are provided purely for illustrative purposes.)
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">wōtōm / otem</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[wɤdˠɤmʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>o͜ɤdˠɤ͜emʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>odˠemʲ]</span> "all; every".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Modern orthography has a bias in certain spelling choices in which both possibilities are equally clear between two non-approximant consonants.
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a</i></span> is preferred over <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā</i></span>.
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧ap</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[lˠɑpʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>lˠɑ͜æpʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>lˠæpʲ]</span> "big", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">l‌̧āp</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> is preferred over <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ū</i></span>.
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">dik</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[rʲik<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>rʲi͜ɯk<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>rʲɯk]</span> "small", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">dūk</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></li>
<li>Historically, both <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ō</i></span> and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> have been common and sometimes interchangeable. It is still true today with some words. In the new orthography, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ō</i></span> is generally preferred over <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> in most such situations.
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">aelōn̄</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑelʲɤŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ɑelʲe͜ɤŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ɑelʲeŋ]</span> "atoll; island; land", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">aelen̄</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-MEDaelon_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDaelon-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Epatōn</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛbʲɑdˠʌnʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ɛbʲæ͜ɑdˠʌ͜ɛnʲ]</span> "<a href="/wiki/Ebadon_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebadon Island">Ebadon</a>", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">Epaten</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kūrijm̧ōj</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kɯrˠizʲĭmˠɤtʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>kɯrˠɯ͜izʲĭ͜ɯ̆mˠɤ͜etʲ]</span> "Christmas", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">Kūrijm̧ej</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Nōl‌̧</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nʲʌlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>nʲɛ͜ʌlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>nʲɛlˠ]</span> "<a href="/wiki/Nell_Island" title="Nell Island">Nell</a>", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">Nel‌̧</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></li>
<li>However, after one of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">d j m p</i></span> and before one of unrounded <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">b k l‌̧ m̧ n‌̧ n̄ r t</i></span>, the spelling <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> is preferred over <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ō</i></span>.
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">pinjel‌̧</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʲinzʲɛlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>pʲinzʲɛ͜ʌlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>pʲinzʲʌlˠ]</span> "pencil", not <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">pinjōl‌̧</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></li>
<li>For the name of the Marshall Islands, the new orthography prefers <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span>, but the spelling with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ō</i></span> is still found.
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">M̧ajel‌̧</i></span> or <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">M̧ajōl‌̧</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mˠɑːzʲɛlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠɑːzʲɛ͜ʌlˠ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>mˠɑːzʲʌlˠ]</span>, "Marshall Islands"<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></li></ul>
<p>In a syllable whose first consonant is rounded and whose second consonant is palatalized, it is common to see the vowel between them written as one of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a ō ū</i></span>, usually associated with a neighboring velarized consonant:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">O̧kwōj</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɒɡʷʌtʲ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ɒɡʷɔ͜ɛtʲ]</span> "August".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Wūjlan̄</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[wɯzʲĭlʲɑŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>u͜izʲĭlʲæ͜ɑŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>uzʲĭlʲɑŋ]</span> "<a href="/wiki/Ujelang" class="mw-redirect" title="Ujelang">Ujelang</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The exception is long vowels and long diphthongs made up of two mora units, which are written with the vowel quality closer to the phonetic nucleus of the long syllable:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jouj</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʲoutʲ]</span> "kindness".<sup id="cite_ref-trussel2.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trussel2.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">naaj</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nʲɑːtʲ]</span> "will be".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">tāākji</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tˠæːɡĭzʲi]</span> "taxicab".<sup id="cite_ref-trussel2.com_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trussel2.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>If the syllable is phonetically open, the vowel written is usually the second vowel in the diphthong: the word <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">bwe</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pˠɛ]</span><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> is usually not written any other way, but exceptions exist such as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">aelōn̄</i></span> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɰajɘlʲɘŋ/<span class="wrap"> </span>[ɑelʲɤŋ]</span> "land; country; island; atoll"<sup id="cite_ref-MEDaelon_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEDaelon-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>), which is preferred over <span title="Marshallese-language text">&#42;<i lang="mh">āelōn̄</i></span> because the <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a</i></span> spelling emphasizes that the first (unwritten) glide phoneme is dorsal rather than palatal.
</p><p>The spelling of grammatical <a href="/wiki/Affix" title="Affix">affixes</a>, such as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ri-</i></span> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rˠi-/</span><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>) and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">-in</i></span> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/-inʲ/</span>) is less variable despite the fact that their vowels become diphthongs with second member dependent on the preceding/following consonant: the prefix <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ri-</i></span> may be pronounced as any of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[rˠɯ͜i,<span class="wrap"> </span>rˠɯ,<span class="wrap"> </span>rˠɯ͜u]</span> depending on the stem. The term <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ri-M̧ajel‌̧</i></span> ("<a href="/wiki/Marshallese_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshallese people">Marshallese people</a>") is actually pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[rˠɯmˠɑːzʲɛlˠ]</span> as if it were <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Rūm̧ajel‌̧</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Display_issues">Display issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Display issues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the most <a href="/wiki/Copy_editing" title="Copy editing">polished</a> printed text, the letters <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">L‌̧ l‌̧ M̧ m̧ N‌̧ n‌̧ O̧ o̧</i></span> always appear with unaltered <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">cedillas</a> directly beneath, and the letters <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ā ā N̄ n̄ Ō ō Ū ū</i></span> always appear with unaltered <a href="/wiki/Macron_(diacritic)" title="Macron (diacritic)">macrons</a> directly above. Regardless, the diacritics are often replaced by ad hoc spellings using more common or more easily displayable characters. In particular, the <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.trussel2.com/MOD/">Marshallese-English Online Dictionary</a></i> (but not the print version), or MOD, uses the following characters:<sup id="cite_ref-MED_36-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table border="0" style="border-collapse:collapse; text-align:center">
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="5">Standard
</th>
<th rowspan="3">&#160;&#160;&#160;
</th>
<th colspan="5">MOD
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">L‌̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">M̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">N‌̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">N̄</i></span></td>

</td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ḷ</i></span></td>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">m̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">n‌̧</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">n̄</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">o̧</i></span>
</td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ḷ</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ṃ</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ṇ</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ñ</i></span></td>
<td><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ọ</i></span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As of 2019, there are no dedicated <a href="/wiki/Precomposed_character" title="Precomposed character">precomposed characters</a> in <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> for the letters <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">M̧ m̧ N̄ n̄ O̧ o̧</i></span>; they must be displayed as plain Latin letters with <a href="/wiki/Combining_character" title="Combining character">combining</a> <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>, and even many Unicode <a href="/wiki/Font" title="Font">fonts</a> will not display the combinations properly and neatly. Although <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">L‌̧ l‌̧ N‌̧ n‌̧</i></span> exist as precomposed characters in Unicode, these letters <i>also</i> do not display properly as Marshallese letters in most Unicode fonts. Unicode defines the letters as having a <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">cedilla</a>, but fonts usually display them with a <a href="/wiki/Comma_below" class="mw-redirect" title="Comma below">comma below</a> because of rendering expectations of the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian alphabet">Latvian alphabet</a>. For many fonts, a workaround is to encode these letters as the base letter <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">L l N n</i></span> followed by a <a href="/wiki/Zero-width_non-joiner" title="Zero-width non-joiner">zero-width non-joiner</a> and then a combining cedilla, producing <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">L‌̧ l‌̧ N‌̧ n‌̧</i></span>. 
</p><p>Both systems already require fonts that display <a href="/wiki/ISO_basic_Latin_alphabet" title="ISO basic Latin alphabet">Basic Latin</a> (with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">A a B b D d E e I i J j K k L l M m N n O o P p R r T t U u W w</i></span>) and <a href="/wiki/Latin_Extended-A" title="Latin Extended-A">Latin Extended-A</a> (with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ā ā Ō ō Ū ū</i></span>). The standard orthography also requires <a href="/wiki/Combining_Diacritical_Marks" title="Combining Diacritical Marks">Combining Diacritical Marks</a> for the combining diacritics. The MOD's alternative letters have the advantage of being neatly displayable as all-precomposed characters in any Unicode fonts that support Basic Latin, Latin Extended-A along with <a href="/wiki/Latin-1_Supplement" title="Latin-1 Supplement">Latin-1 Supplement</a> (with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ñ ñ</i></span>) and <a href="/wiki/Latin_Extended_Additional" title="Latin Extended Additional">Latin Extended Additional</a> (with <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ḷ ḷ Ṃ ṃ Ṇ ṇ Ọ ọ</i></span>). If a font comfortably displays both the <a href="/wiki/International_Alphabet_of_Sanskrit_Transliteration" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">Vietnamese alphabet</a>, it can also display MOD Marshallese.
</p><p>This chart highlights the display issues in common web fonts and common free Unicode fonts that are known to support standard or MOD Marshallese lettering. Distinct typefaces appear only if the operating environment supports them. Some fonts have combining diacritic alignment issues, and the vast majority of the fonts have the Latvian diacritic issue; of the fonts shown below, only the <a href="/wiki/Noto" title="Noto">Noto</a> series displays Marshallese correctly.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_in_orthography">Differences in orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Differences in orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The old orthography was still very similar to the new orthography but made fewer phonological distinctions in spelling than the new orthography does. The new orthography attempts phonological consistency while adhering to most of the spelling patterns of the old orthography, especially in regard to vowels and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">w</i></span>. It has made the new orthography relatively easy for old orthography users to learn. The phonology of Marshallese was documented by Bender (1969) with written examples using the old orthography. Here are some differences between the new and old orthographies:
</p>
<ul><li>The new orthography uses the <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">cedillaed</a> letters <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧ m̧ n‌̧ o̧</i></span>. The old orthography did not use cedillas and ambiguously wrote them <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l m n o</i></span>.</li>
<li>The new orthography uses <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">p</i></span> for "light" <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʲ/</span> and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">b</i></span> for "heavy" <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pˠ/</span>. The old orthography used <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">b</i></span> for both.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">binjel</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">pinjel‌̧</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʲinzʲɛlˠ]</span>, 'pencil'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>The new orthography consistently uses <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">d</i></span> for "light" <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rʲ/</span> in all positions. The old orthography often wrote <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">dr</i></span> before vowels, and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">r</i></span> after vowels.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Amerka</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Amedka</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑmʲɛrʲɛ̆ɡɑ]</span>, '<a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>'.</dd>
<dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">indreo</i></span> or <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">indrio</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">indeeo</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[inrʲeːɔ]</span>, 'forever'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>Except in certain affixes like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">-an</i></span> whose spelling may be fixed, the new orthography spells the vowel monophthong allophone <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">æ</a>&#93;</span> as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā</i></span> in all positions. The old orthography had <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ā</i></span>, but it was relatively less common, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">æ</a>&#93;</span> was sometimes written <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> instead.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ebeje</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Epjā</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛbʲɛ̆zʲæ]</span>, '<a href="/wiki/Ebeye_Island" title="Ebeye Island">Ebeye</a>'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>Except in certain affixes like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ri-</i></span> whose the spelling of the vowels may be fixed, the new orthography spells the vowel monophthong allophone <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Close back unrounded vowel">ɯ</a>&#93;</span> as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ū</i></span> in all positions. The old orthography spelled <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Close back unrounded vowel">ɯ</a>&#93;</span> as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> between consonants.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kirijmōj</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kūrijm̧ōj</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kɯrˠizʲĭmˠɤtʲ]</span>, 'Christmas'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>The new orthography uses only <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e o ō</i></span> for allophones of the vowel phoneme <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span>. In the old orthography, some words used <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e o ō</i></span>, but other words used <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i u (ū)</i></span> instead.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ailin̄</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">aelōn̄</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑelʲɤŋ<span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span>ɑelʲeŋ]</span>, 'land'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>The new orthography uses the letter <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">o̧</i></span> for the vowel monophthong allophone <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">ɒ</a>&#93;</span> along with many of its related diphthong allophones. The old orthography spelt <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">ɒ</a>&#93;</span> as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">a</i></span> between consonants but <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">o</i></span> at the ends of words.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">iakwe</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i̯ɒɡʷɛ]</span>, 'hello; good bye; love'.</dd>
<dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">mo</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">mo̧</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mʲɒ]</span>, 'taboo'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>The new orthography tries to consistently write long vowels and geminated consonants with double letters. The old orthography habitually wrote these as single letters.
<dl><dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ekatak</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ekkatak</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛkːɑdˠɑk]</span>, 'study'.</dd>
<dd>Compare old <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jab</i></span> vs. new <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jaab</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʲɑːpˠ]</span>, 'no'.</dd></dl></li>
<li>The word <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i̯ɒɡʷɛ]</span> ('hello; goodbye; love') and the phrase <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe eok</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i̯ɒɡʷɛe̯okʷ]</span> ('hello [to you]') are a special case. The new orthography's rules use <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe eok</i></span>, while the old orthography's rules used <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">iakwe iuk</i></span>. However, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">yokwe yuk</i></span> has been historically more entrenched in both orthographies, but the letter <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">y</i></span> does not exist in the normal spelling rules of either orthography. That spelling has multilingual significance as well; <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">yokwe (yuk)</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈjɒkweɪ<span class="wrap"> </span>(ˈjʊk)/</span> is also the established spelling for the greeting when used in Marshallese-influenced <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and by <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">anglophones</a> in the Marshall Islands.</li></ul>
<h2><span id="Bender.27s_orthography"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bender's_orthography">Bender's orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bender&#039;s orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In his 1968 publication <i>Marshallese Phonology</i>, linguist <a href="/wiki/Byron_W._Bender" title="Byron W. Bender">Byron W. Bender</a> designed a purely morphophonemic orthography, containing only non-IPA symbols corresponding to consonant phonemes, vowel phonemes and regular reflexes between the dialects, intended for use in dictionaries and language teaching. Besides also appearing in his 1969 tutorial <i>Spoken Marshallese</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBender1969&#91;&#91;Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021&#93;&#93;&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;&#91;&#91;Wikipedia:Citing_sources&#124;&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;&#93;&#93;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBender1969[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> it appeared in a modified form alongside the "new" orthography in the 1976 <i>Marshallese-English Dictionary</i> (MED) to which he contributed. Bender later collaborated with Stephen Trussel when the MED was adapted to website format as the <i>Marshallese-English Online Dictionary</i> (MOD), with Bender's orthography appearing in an again-modified form.
</p>

<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>
</td></tr>

<p>The MOD's version of Bender's orthography uses <a href="/wiki/Dot_(diacritic)" title="Dot (diacritic)">under-dot</a> diacritics instead of the <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">cedillas</a> used both by the "new" orthography and by the 1976 MED's version of Bender's orthography, for reasons specific to the MOD's <a href="#Display_issues">display issues</a>.
</p><p>In addition to plain sequences of phonemes, Bender's orthography recognizes a few special sequences, many of which relate to regular differences between the <a href="/wiki/Ralik_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ralik Chain">Rālik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ratak_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ratak Chain">Ratak</a> dialects of Marshallese.
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yi'y&#125;</i></span> is for a "passing over lightly" version of the vowel allophone <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> that occurs at the beginning of certain words, phonetically pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">i̯</a>&#93;</span> and existing on the phonemic level as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ji̯j/</span>. For example, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yi'yakʷey&#125;</i></span> is equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">io̧kwe</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i̯ɒɡʷɛ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/ji̯jækʷɛj/</span> "hello; goodbye; love".</li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;'yiy&#125;</i></span> is for a "dwelling upon" version of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> that occurs at the beginning of certain words, now generally written <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ii</i></span> in the "new" orthography, phonetically pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">iː</a>&#93;</span> and existing on the phonemic level as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jijj/</span>, effectively making it identical to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiyy&#125;</i></span>. An example is <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;'yiyayiyȩw&#125;</i></span>, which is equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">iiāio</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iːæio]<span class="wrap"> </span>/jijjæjijew/</span> "reunion".</li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiy&#125;</i></span> at the beginning of a word, without apostrophes, indicates a version of <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">i</i></span> whose reflex differs between the two dialects. In the Rālik dialect, this assumes the "dwelling upon" pronunciation, equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;'yiy&#125;</i></span>. In the Ratak dialect, it instead assumes the "passing over lightly" pronunciation, equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yi'y&#125;</i></span>. An example is <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiyal‌̧&#125;</i></span>, equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ial‌̧</i></span> "road":
<ul><li>In the Rālik dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiyal‌̧&#125;</i></span> becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iːɑlˠ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/jijjælˠ/</span> and is often instead written as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">iial‌̧</i></span> in the "new" orthography.</li>
<li>In the Ratak dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiyal‌̧&#125;</i></span> becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[i̯ɑlˠ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/ji̯jælˠ/</span>.</li></ul></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hhV&#125;</i></span> at the beginning of a word (where "V" can be any vowel) indicates a back unrounded vowel that whose reflex differs between the dialects. In the Rālik dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hhV&#125;</i></span> becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hVhV&#125;</i></span>, lengthening the vowel. In the Ratak dialect, the second <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;h&#125;</i></span> disappears, becoming <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hV&#125;</i></span>, and the vowel remains short. An example is <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hhayȩt</i></span>, equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">aet</i></span> "yes":
<ul><li>In the Rālik dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hhayȩt&#125;</i></span> becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑːetˠ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/ɰæɰæjetˠ/</span> and is often instead written as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">aaet</i></span> in the "new" orthography.</li>
<li>In the Ratak dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hhayȩt&#125;</i></span> becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑetˠ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/ɰæjetˠ/</span>.</li></ul></li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiwV&#125;</i></span> at the beginning of a word (where "V" can be any vowel) is usually equivalent to <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiwwV&#125;</i></span>.</li>
<li><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;wiwV&#125;</i></span> at the beginning of a word (where "V" can be any vowel) usually becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yiwwV&#125;</i></span> in the Rālik dialect, but usually becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;wiwwV&#125;</i></span> in the Ratak dialect.</li>
<li>When a Bender orthography spelling begins with a doubled consonant other than <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;hh&#125;</i></span>, such as <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> "good", its reflex differs between the dialects.
<ul><li>In the Rālik dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;yem̧m̧an&#125;</i></span>, sprouting both a <a href="/wiki/Prothesis_(linguistics)" title="Prothesis (linguistics)">prothetic</a> <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;y&#125;</i></span> and a vowel. The dialect generally spells this <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">em̧m̧an</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛmˠːɑnʲ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/jemˠmˠænʲ/</span> "good" in the "new" orthography, making it homophonous with the phrase <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">em̧m̧an</i></span> which means "it is good" in both dialects.</li>
<li>In the Ratak dialect, <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧em̧an&#125;</i></span> with only a prothetic vowel, appearing instead between the two consonants. The dialect generally spells this <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">m̧ōm̧an</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mˠʌmˠɑnʲ]<span class="wrap"> </span>/mˠɛmˠænʲ/</span> "good" in the "new" orthography.</li>
<li>In both dialects, the prothetic vowel is equivalent to the first stem vowel unless it is <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;a&#125;</i></span>, in which case the stem vowel is always paired with the prothetic vowel <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;e&#125;</i></span>. But when spellings like <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> take <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefixes</a> with a vowel, there are no prothetic vowels: <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;ri-&#125;</i></span> "person" + <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;m̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> "good" becomes <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">&#123;rim̧m̧an&#125;</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rˠi-mˠmˠænʲ/<span class="wrap"> </span>[rˠɯmˠːɑnʲ]</span>, which the "new" orthography spells <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">rūm̧m̧an</i></span> "good person".</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">Morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Morphology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nouns are not marked as nouns, and do not inflect for number, gender, or case.<sup id="cite_ref-ws15_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws15-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Nouns are often verbalized and verbs nominalized without any overt morphological marker:<sup id="cite_ref-ws15_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws15-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Je-n</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1PL</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inclusive person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="agreement" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AGR</abbr>-should</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">al</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sing.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="transitive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">TR</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">al</p><p style="margin: 0px;">song</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">in</p><p style="margin: 0px;">of</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pālle.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be.covered(=American)</p></div><p style="display: none;">Je-n al al in pālle.</p><p style="display: none;">1PL.IN.AGR-should sing.TR song of be.covered(=American)</p><p style="clear: left;">'We should sing American songs.' (Willson 2008)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Marshallese has determiners and demonstratives which follow the noun they modify.<sup id="cite_ref-ws16_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws16-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> These are marked for number, and in the plural also encode a human/nonhuman distinction.<sup id="cite_ref-ws17_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws17-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> For example, in the singular <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">pinjel‌̧ eo</i></span> 'the pencil' and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧addik eo</i></span> 'the boy' take the same determiner, but in the plural <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">pinjel‌̧ ko</i></span> 'the pencils' and <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧addik ro</i></span> have different determiners.<sup id="cite_ref-ws17_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws17-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Indefinites are an exception; in the singular they are expressed with the word <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">juon</i></span> 'one' before the noun (e.g. <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">juon al</i></span> 'a song'), and there is no plural indefinite determiner.<sup id="cite_ref-ws17-18_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws17-18-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Marshallese demonstrative system has five levels:
</p>
<ol><li>near the speaker (sg. <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">e</i></span> / pl. human <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">rā</i></span> / pl. nonhuman <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kā</i></span>)</li>
<li>near the speaker and listener (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">in / rein / kein</i></span>)</li>
<li>near the listener (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">n‌̧e / ran‌̧e / kan‌̧e</i></span>)</li>
<li>away from both speaker and listener (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">en‌̧ / ran‌̧ / kan‌̧</i></span>)</li>
<li>distant but visible (<span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">uweo / roro / koko</i></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-ws17_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws17-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<div style="float:right; margin-left:20px">
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">

</td></tr>

</th>
<th>1
</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Clusivity" title="Clusivity">inc</a>
</th>
<td colspan="2"><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kōj</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>1
</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Clusivity" title="Clusivity">exc</a>
</th>
<td colspan="2"><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kōm</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2">2
</th>
<td colspan="2"><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kom̧</i></span> (Ralik)<br /><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kom̧i</i></span> (Ratak)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2">3
</th>
<td colspan="2"><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">er</i></span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</div>
<p>Marshallese possesses two sets of 1st and 2nd person singular pronouns, known as "absolutive" or "emphatic" pronouns and as "objective" pronouns.<sup id="cite_ref-ws18_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws18-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Marshallese 1st person plurals mark for <a href="/wiki/Clusivity" title="Clusivity">clusivity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ws18_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws18-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Third person objective pronouns may only be used for humans; nonhumans instead take a null pronoun:<sup id="cite_ref-ws18_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws18-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">E-ar</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="agreement" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AGR</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">den̄ōt</p><p style="margin: 0px;">slap.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="transitive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">TR</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">er.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, plural" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3PL</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="object pronoun" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">OBJ</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">E-ar den̄ōt er.</p><p style="display: none;">3S.AGR-PAST slap.TR 3PL.<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="object pronoun" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">OBJ</abbr></p><p style="clear: left;">'He slapped them (human).' (Willson 2008)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">E-ar</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="agreement" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AGR</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">den̄ōt-i.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">slap.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="transitive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">TR</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="object marker" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">OBJ</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">E-ar den̄ōt-i.</p><p style="display: none;">3S.AGR-PAST slap.TR-<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="object marker" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">OBJ</abbr></p><p style="clear: left;">'He slapped them (nonhuman).' (Willson 2008)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The emphatic pronouns serve as subjects of equational sentences, as complements of prepositions, in order to emphasize objects, in coordination structures, and with topicalized or focused subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-ws19-21_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws19-21-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> It is common in Oceanic languages for a special type of pronoun to be used in equational sentences and for topicalization or focus.<sup id="cite_ref-ws19-21_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws19-21-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">N̄a</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="emphatic" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">EMPH</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">rikaki.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">teacher</p></div><p style="display: none;">N̄a rikaki.</p><p style="display: none;">1S.EMPH teacher</p><p style="clear: left;">'I am a teacher.' (Willson 2008)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">N̄a</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="emphatic" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">EMPH</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">i-j</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="agreement" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AGR</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRES</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">yokwe</p><p style="margin: 0px;">love</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ajiri</p><p style="margin: 0px;">child</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ro</p><p style="margin: 0px;">the.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="human/anthropic gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">HUM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nej-ū.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessive classifier for cherished items" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CHER.POSS</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1S</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="genitive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">GEN</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">N̄a i-j yokwe ajiri ro nej-ū.</p><p style="display: none;">1S.EMPH 1S.AGR.PRES love child the.PL.HUM <abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessive classifier for cherished items" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CHER.POSS</abbr>-1S.GEN</p><p style="clear: left;">'Me, I love my children.' (Willson 2008)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Marshallese has four verb tenses: present, past, near future, and future. The tenses are formed by adding a tense suffix to the personal pronoun in the sentence. If the subject is not a personal pronoun, a third-person pronoun is added with the appropriate tense suffix. The present tense is formed by attaching the suffix -j to the personal pronoun (-ij for kōm and kom̧). The suffix for the past tense is either -ar or -kar depending on the dialect. -naaj is the suffix used for the regular future tense and -itōn is used for the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERudiak-Gould200435_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERudiak-Gould200435-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">Syntax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Syntax"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Marshallese, like many Micronesian languages, divides sentences into two types: predicational sentences and equational sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-wms_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wms-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Predicational sentences have <a href="/wiki/Subject-verb-object" class="mw-redirect" title="Subject-verb-object">SVO</a> word order and a main verb:<sup id="cite_ref-wms_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wms-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">E-j</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRES</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kajan̄jan̄</p><p style="margin: 0px;">play</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kita.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">guitar.</p></div><p style="display: none;">E-j kajan̄jan̄ kita.</p><p style="display: none;">3S-PRES play guitar.</p><p style="clear: left;">'He plays guitar.' (Willson 2002)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>In equational sentences, both the subject and predicate are noun phrases:<sup id="cite_ref-wms_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wms-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Nuknuk</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dress</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">eo</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="determiner" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DET</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="mh" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">e-aibujuij.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>-beautiful.</p></div><p style="display: none;">Nuknuk eo e-aibujuij.</p><p style="display: none;">dress DET 3S-beautiful.</p><p style="clear: left;">'The dress is beautiful.' (Willson 2002)</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardinal_numbers">Cardinal numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cardinal numbers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This includes the cardinal numbers one through ten in the Rālik dialect. Where Ratak forms differ, they are listed in parentheses.
</p>
<ol><li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">juon</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[tʲuɔnʲ]</a></span></li>
<li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ruo</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[rˠuɔ]</a></span></li>
<li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jilu</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[tʲilʲu]</a></span></li>
<li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">emān</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[ɛmʲænʲ]</a></span></li>
<li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l‌̧alem</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[lˠɑlʲemʲ]</a></span></li>
<li><b><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">jiljino</i></span></b> <span class="IPA" lang="mh-Latn-fonipa" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Marshallese" title="Help:IPA/Marshallese">[tʲizʲinʲɔ]</a></span> (the <span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">l</i></span> is silent<sup id="cite_ref-r12_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r12-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Text_examples">Text examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Text examples"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_orthography">Modern orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Modern orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Here is the <a href="/wiki/Hail_Mary" title="Hail Mary">Hail Mary</a> in standard Marshallese orthography:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Io̧kwe eok Maria, kwo lōn̄ kōn</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">menin jouj;</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Irooj ej pād ippam̧.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kwo jeram̧m̧an iaan kōrā ran‌̧ im</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">ejeram̧m̧an ineen lo̧jiōm̧, Jesus.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">O Maria kwojarjar, jinen Anij,</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">kwōn jar kōn kem rijjerawiwi.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kiiō im ilo iien</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">amwōj mej. Amen.</i></span></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Older_orthography">Older orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marshallese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Older orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Here is the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Lord's Prayer</a> from the 1982 Marshallese Bible, which uses the older orthography:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Jememuij iljōn̄:</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">En kwojarjar im utiej etam;</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">En itok am Ailin̄;</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Kimin kōmōnmōn ankilam ilōl einwōt air kōmmōn ilōn.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Letok n̄ōn kim kijim rainin.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Jolok amuij bwid ibbam,</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Einwōt kimij julok bwid ko an ro jet ibbem.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Am melejjon̄e kim en jab ellā jen jon̄an,</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Ak kwon kejbarok kim jen Eo Enana.</i></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Marshallese-language text"><i lang="mh">Bwe am Ailin̄ im kajur im aibuijuij indrio, Amen.</i></span></dd></dl>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.linguistics.berkeley.edu/~rscook/pdf/PCMLT-JejeinM.pdf">Peace Corps Marshall Islands <i>Marshallese Language Training Manual</i></a> (<a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Document Format">PDF</a>, 275 KB; instead of macrons uses trema on vowels and tilde on <i>n</i>, and underlines instead of cedillas)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://faroutliers.blogspot.com/2004/08/marshallese-spelling-reforms.html">Marshallese Spelling Reforms</a> article in the blog, "Far Outliers"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kaipuleohone" title="Kaipuleohone">Kaipuleohone</a> has recordings of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://scholarspace.manoa.hawaii.edu/handle/10125/27416">stories from the 1950s</a> as well as <a href="http://hdl.handle.net/10125/32782" class="extiw" title="hdl:10125/32782">index cards of plant and animal words</a></li>
<li>Materials on Marshallese are included in the open access <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Capell" title="Arthur Capell">Arthur Capell</a> collections (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://catalog.paradisec.org.au/collections/AC1">AC1</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://catalog.paradisec.org.au/collections/AC2">AC2</a>) held by <a href="/wiki/Paradisec" title="Paradisec">Paradisec</a></li></ul>
